CellCell Font:NameFont:Name
CellCell Font:NameFont:Name

The name of the font in all cells. Predefined font names include App Font, Sys
Font, and Dlg Font.

This property is an element of the Cell Font property.

If you select an invalid font, this property returns an error.

Remarks

The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


 Data type

 Permissions                                                          Read/Write

 Available in Run-Time Engine                                             Yes

 Need to authenticate before use                            No

 Loads the block diagram into memory                        No

 Remote access allowed                                             Yes

EditEdit PositionPosition
EditEdit PositionPosition

The row-column pair index of the current text entry. Values of (0,0) indicate the top-left
text entry. A value of –1 indicates the row header but it cannot be edited using this
property. Values of (–2, –2) indicate that no edits are being made to the text of the
control.

Before you use this property to set text focus on a control, set key focus of the control.


                                                    © National Instruments 8509

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8509 -->

   SelectionSelection ColorColor
    SelectionSelection ColorColor

       Color to use to highlight the data selection.

      You can set the color of the front panel object by wiring a hexadecimal number with
       the form RRGGBB or by wiring the color box constant to the property.

SelectionSelection SizeSize
SelectionSelection SizeSize

Index of the row and column pair that specifies the number of rows and columns in the
selection.

Elements

 Name   Description

         Index of the row that specifies the total number of rows in the selection. Valid values
 Row
          include 0 through n-1, where nis the total number of rows in the digital table.

         Index of the column that specifies the total number of columns in the selection. Valid
 Column          values include 0 through m-1, where mis the total number of columns in the digital table.

Remarks

The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


 Data type

 Permissions                                                          Read/Write

 Available in Run-Time Engine                                             Yes

 Available in Real-Time Operating System                                  Yes

 Settable when the VI is running                                           Yes

 Loads the front panel into memory                              No

 Need to authenticate before use                                No

 Loads the block diagram into memory                            No

 Remote access allowed                                                  Yes

   TopTop LeftLeft CellCell
   TopTop LeftLeft CellCell

      The row and column of the cell displayed in the top left corner of the table. Use this
       property to read or change the top item, or use it to read or change the leftmost
      column of information displayed.

       This property returns the row and column of the cell at the top left corner of the visible
       table window, which is not necessarily the top left item of the table. To access the top
         left item, wire a value of (0,0) to the Active Cell property.

     Elements

      Name     Description

      Row      The row index of the cell displayed in the top left corner of the table.

       Column   The column index of the cell displayed in the top left corner of the table.

     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


        Data type

         Permissions                                                          Read/Write

         Available in Run-Time Engine                                             Yes

         Available in Real-Time Operating System                                  Yes

         Settable when the VI is running                                           Yes

8518   ni.com

   ValueValue
   ValueValue

       Value of digital data control.

     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


        Data type

         Permissions                                                          Read/Write

         Available in Run-Time Engine                                             Yes

         Available in Real-Time Operating System                                  Yes

         Settable when the VI is running                                           Yes

        Loads the front panel into memory                              No

       Need to authenticate before use                                No

        Loads the block diagram into memory                            No

       Remote access allowed                                                  Yes

   ValueValue (Signaling)(Signaling)
   ValueValue (Signaling)(Signaling)

       Sets the value of the control and generates a Value Change event.

       This property updates the value of an object similar to the Value property. However,
       Value (Signaling) also causes LabVIEW to generate an event as if the user had
        interactively changed the value of the object. National Instruments recommends you
      use this property only when you rely on LabVIEW generating an event in response to
       the programmatic value change.

8520   ni.com

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8520 -->

       Method         Description

       Custom Item    Returns the item symbol as a cluster of image data so you can draw it as a picture
        Symbols:Get    using the Draw Flattened Pixmap VI or save the image to a file using the Graphics
       Symbol        Formats VIs.

        Symbols:Get    them as pictures using the Draw Flattened Pixmap VI or save the images to files

        Symbols:Revert

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


Method         Description

Custom
Symbol

Custom Item
Symbols:Set To                Sets the images of all item symbols.
Custom
Symbol Array

                Returns the unique tag of the last item the user double-clicked or returns an
Double Click    empty string if the user did not double-click an item since you last called this
              method.

Edit Tree       Adds an item to the tree control. This method returns a unique tag for the new
Items:Add Item  item.

Edit Tree
Items:Add Item  Adds an item after all existing items in the tree control.
to End

Edit Tree
Items:Add              Adds items after all existing items in the tree control.Multiple Items
to End

Edit Tree
                Deletes an item from the tree control. Wire an empty string to tag and a value ofItems:Delete             TRUE to Delete Children to delete all items in the tree control.Item

Edit Tree
Items:Move     Moves an existing item to a new position in the tree control.
Item

Edit Tree        Sets the unique tag of a tree control item, which you use to modify the item or to
Items:Set Tag    gather information about the item programmatically.

Edit Tree
Items:Sort       Sorts the child items under an item alphabetically.
Children

Navigate        Returns the tag of the first child item under an item. If the item has no child items,
Tree:Get Child   the method returns an empty string.

Navigate        Returns the tag of the first item after an item at the same level in the hierarchy. If
Tree:Get Next   no items exist after the item at the same level in the hierarchy, the method returns
Item          an empty string.

Navigate        Returns the tag of the parent item above an item. If the item is the topmost item in

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


       Method         Description

         Tree:Get Parent                        the tree control, the method returns an empty string.        Item

         Navigate        Returns an array of unique tags for each item in the path from the root level in the
         Tree:Get Path    tree control to the item.

         Navigate        Returns the tag of the item immediately before and at the same hierarchical level
         Tree:Get        as the one you provide as an input. If no items exist before the item at the same
         Previous Item    level in the hierarchy, this method returns an empty string.

         Open/Close:All  Expands or closes all nodes in the tree control.

        Open/                            Scrolls to an item and if necessary, expands nodes in the tree control to make the         Close:Ensure                        item visible.          Visible

        Open/                      Expands or closes a node in the tree control.         Close:Item

                        Converts a pixel coordinate to a tag-column pair in the coordinates of the control.
                          This method also returns whether the point is inside the bounds of the content
         Point to Row                          rectangle and whether the point is within the custom symbol of the cell. The
       Column                    method returns the tag TREE_COLUMN_HEADERS when you wire a point that is
                         within the tree's column headers.

   CustomCustom ItemItem Symbols:GetSymbols:Get SymbolSymbol
   CustomCustom ItemItem Symbols:GetSymbols:Get SymbolSymbol

       Returns the item symbol as a cluster of image data so you can draw it as a picture
       using the Draw Flattened Pixmap VI or save the image to a file using the Graphics
      Formats VIs.

      The cluster returned by this method is similar to the image data output of the Read
      JPEG File, Read PNG File, and Read BMP File VIs.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


              Data      Name       Required  Description
               type

                                                  • Child Text—Array of strings to display in the remaining cells for the
                            new item. The default is an array of empty strings.
                                                  • Child Tag—Unique tag for the new item. The default is the string you
                                    wire to Left Cell String. If an existing tag already uses that string,
                                LabVIEW appends a number to the string to create a unique tag for
                                   the new item. You cannot create a tag that begins with TREE_. All
                                     tags that begin with TREE_ are reserved for use by LabVIEW. If the tag
                                you wire to the method begins with TREE_, LabVIEW prepends an
                                   underscore (_) to create a valid tag for the new item. If the tag you
                                    wire to the method begins or ends with white space or non-printing
                                       characters, such as a tab or new line, LabVIEW removes the white
                                  space or non-printing characters.
                                                  • Item Indent—The level in the hierarchy at which to place the new
                                      item. Wire a value of 0 (default) to place the new item at the highest
                                         level in the hierarchy, wire a value of 1 to indent the new item one
                                            level, and so on. If the value you wire to this input would indent the
                            new item more than one level under its parent item, the method
                                      returns an error.
                                                  • Child Only?—If TRUE, you cannot indent other items under the new
                                      item. The default is FALSE. This property is similar to the Child-Only
                                  Item item on the shortcut menu of a tree control.
                                                  • Glyph Index—An integer representing the symbol index associated
                                   with the item.

EditEdit TreeTree Items:DeleteItems:Delete ItemItem
EditEdit TreeTree Items:DeleteItems:Delete ItemItem

Deletes an item from the tree control. Wire an empty string to tag and a value of TRUE
to Delete Children to delete all items in the tree control.

If you do not update the value of a tree control after deleting a row, the control may
return old data. Deleting a selected item does not change the value of a tree control.
After you delete an item, the tree value may be a tag for an item that no longer exists.
You can select one of the remaining tree items to update the value of the tree control.

This method is similar to the Delete Item item on the shortcut menu of a tree control.

Parameters

          Data
 Name          Required  Description          type

                        Unique tag of the item you want to delete. The default is an empty
 Tag          No                                 string, which represents the root level in the tree control.


                                            If TRUE (default), the method deletes all the child items under the item
 Delete                  you want to delete. If FALSE, the method moves all the child items to
             No
 Children?                    level in the hierarchy of the item you want to delete before deleting
                           the item.


Remarks

The following table lists the characteristics of this method.


                                                    © National Instruments 8537

       Remote access allowed                                                           Yes

     Examples

       Refer to the following example files included with LabVIEW.

            • labview\examples\Controls and Indicators\Tree\Setting
        Custom Tree Item Symbols.vi

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

PointPoint toto RowRow ColumnColumn
PointPoint toto RowRow ColumnColumn

Converts a pixel coordinate to a tag-column pair in the coordinates of the control. This
method also returns whether the point is inside the bounds of the content rectangle
and whether the point is within the custom symbol of the cell. The method returns the
tag TREE_COLUMN_HEADERS when you wire a point that is within the tree's column
headers.

      Note The Point to Row Column method does not return an error for points
        that lie within a control but outside of the actual cell area for that control,
       such as the scroll bar. Use the InBounds parameter to verify that a point lies
        within the cell area of a control.

Parameters

          Data Name             Required  Description          type

 Point              Yes        Specifies the pixel coordinate to translate into a tag-column pair.


 In                           Returns TRUE if the point is inside the bounds of the content                    Yes
 Bounds?                       rectangle.


 Tag                Yes       Returns the tag of the cell in which the point lies.


 Column            Yes       Returns the column of the cell in which the point lies.


 In                           Returns TRUE if the point is within the bounds of the custom
                    Yes
 Symbol?                   symbol of the cell.


                                                    © National Instruments 8551

                            If TRUE, LabVIEW automatically accepts drops containing the LV_TREE_TAG,

                    string that represents the tag from which you drag. The LV_TEXT data type is of
Drag/Drop:Allow  type string. The LV_TREE_ITEMS data type is an array of a cluster containing
Dropping       an array of strings, from left to right, in the item you are dragging, an integer

  • labview\examples\Controls and Indicators\Tree\Tree.vi
ActiveActive Item:Child-Only?Item:Child-Only?
ActiveActive Item:Child-Only?Item:Child-Only?

If TRUE, you cannot indent other items under the active item(s).

If the active item is the column headers or if the active item has other items indented
under it, this property returns an error. If the active item is all rows, the property
returns an error.

This property is similar to the Child-Only Item item on the shortcut menu of a tree
control.

Remarks

The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


 Data type

   ActiveActive Item:Disabled?Item:Disabled?
    ActiveActive Item:Disabled?Item:Disabled?

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

If the active item is the column headers, this property returns an error. If the active
item is all rows, this property returns an error.

If you wire a value to this property that is more than one level greater than the indent
level of the item above the item you want to indent, this property returns an error.

This property is similar to the Indent Item and Outdent Item items on the shortcut
menu of a tree control.

    ActiveActive Item:RowItem:Row NumberNumber

      The row number of the item to which you want to apply subsequent property changes.
       Wire a value of –1 to this property to select the column headers. Wire a value of –2 to

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

When you write to this property, this property sets the active item to the row number
you specify. This property returns an error if you specify an invalid row number. An
invalid row is an empty row below the tree.

AllowAllow SelectionSelection ofof ParentParent ItemsItems
AllowAllow SelectionSelection ofof ParentParent ItemsItems

If TRUE, users can select items that have other items indented under them and items
that are not child-only and do not have other items indented under them. If FALSE,
users can select only items with a value of TRUE for the Child-Only? property.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

   AutosizingAutosizing RowRow HeightHeight
    AutosizingAutosizing RowRow HeightHeight

      Determines whether the rows autosize their height to display all text when fonts
      change or when the number of lines in a cell changes.

           If FALSE, you can have clipped text in cells, and the user will be unable to manually
        resize the row height at run time to see all of the text. This property affects only user
       input. If you use the Value property to set the item strings, the rows do not
       automatically resize. To resize the rows, set this property to FALSE and then set it back
       to TRUE.

       This property is similar to the Autosize Row Height item on the shortcut menu of a tree
        control.

     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


        Data type

         Permissions                                                          Read/Write

         Available in Run-Time Engine                                             Yes

         Available in Real-Time Operating System                                  Yes

         Settable when the VI is running                                           Yes

        Loads the front panel into memory                              No

       Need to authenticate before use                                No

        Loads the block diagram into memory                            No

       Remote access allowed                                                  Yes


8580   ni.com

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8580 -->

other controls.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


 Data type

 Permissions                                                          Read/Write

 Available in Run-Time Engine                                             Yes

 Available in Real-Time Operating System                                  Yes

 Settable when the VI is running                                           Yes

 Loads the front panel into memory                              No

 Need to authenticate before use                                No

 Loads the block diagram into memory                            No

 Remote access allowed                                                  Yes

Drag/Drop:AllowDrag/Drop:Allow DroppingDropping
Drag/Drop:AllowDrag/Drop:Allow DroppingDropping

If TRUE, LabVIEW automatically accepts drops containing the LV_TREE_TAG,
LV_TEXT, or LV_TREE_ITEMS data types. The LV_TREE_TAG data type is a string
that represents the tag from which you drag. The LV_TEXT data type is of type string.
The LV_TREE_ITEMS data type is an array of a cluster containing an array of strings,
from left to right, in the item you are dragging, an integer representing the glyph index
associated with the item from which you are dragging data, and an integer
representing the indent level of the item from which you are dragging.

Use the Control events for more control over how users drag items within controls.

This property is similar to the Allow Dropping item on the shortcut menu of a tree
control.

Remarks

The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


 Data type


                                                    © National Instruments 8589

Drag/Drop:DragDrag/Drop:Drag ModeMode
Drag/Drop:DragDrag/Drop:Drag ModeMode

Sets the default behavior for a drag and drop operation for the control. The settings
apply only when the control configured is the source of the drag and drop operation.

Use the Control events for more control over how users drag and drop items within
controls.

This property is similar to the Drag Mode item on the shortcut menu of a tree control.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

   EditEdit PositionPosition
    EditEdit PositionPosition

      The row-column pair index of the current text entry. Values of (0,0) indicate the top-left
        text entry. A value of –1 indicates the row or column header but they cannot be edited
       using this property. Values of (–2, –2) indicate that no edits are being made to the text
       of the control.

       Before you use this property to set text focus on a control, set key focus of the control.

     Elements

      Name   Description
               The row of the current text entry. Possible values are 0…n, where nis the total number of      Row
                rows - 1.
               The column of the current text entry. Possible values are 0…m, where mis the total       Column
              number of columns - 1.

     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


        Data type

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

Expand/ContractExpand/Contract Symbol:ShowSymbol:Show SymbolSymbol
atat RootRoot
Expand/ContractExpand/Contract Symbol:ShowSymbol:Show SymbolSymbol atat
RootRoot

Shows or hides the expand/contract symbols for items at indent level 0. The indent
level 0 items become flush with the left side of the tree control when you hide the
expand/contract symbols.

If you hide the expand/contract symbols, you can still expand or collapse an item at
indent level 0 by double-clicking the item.

To disable the double-clicking functionality, wire a True constant to the Discard?
parameter of the Item Close? event.

Remarks

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

MultipleMultiple LineLine InputInput
MultipleMultiple LineLine InputInput

If TRUE, you can enter multiple lines of text in the tree control cells by pressing the
<Enter> key on the keyboard. If FALSE, pressing the <Enter> key on the keyboard while
editing cells causes LabVIEW to commit the edits in the current cell and the text focus
moves to the next cell. This property does not affect run-time behavior of the tree
control.

This property is similar to the Multi-line Input item on the shortcut menu of a tree
control.

Remarks

The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


 Data type

   NumberNumber ofof ColumnsColumns
   NumberNumber ofof ColumnsColumns

     Number of visible columns in the tree control. This property counts partially visible
      columns.

           If you wire a value of 0 to this property, LabVIEW displays the leftmost column. The
       tree control resizes according to the number of columns you set.

    SiblingSibling MultiselectMultiselect
    SiblingSibling MultiselectMultiselect

           If TRUE and the Selection Mode is 0 or More Items, users can select multiple items only
           if those items are siblings.

           If you enable Sibling Multiselect, but there are multiple non-sibling items already
       selected, subsequent selection behavior might not be intuitive. If you reset the
       selection to something valid, the selection behavior returns to normal.

       This property is similar to the Selection Mode»Limit Multiselect to Siblings item on the

<!--KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8606 ordinal=8606 -->
## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

           If you wire a tag of TREE_COLUMN_HEADERS or TREE_ALL_ROWS or a column of –2
       to this property, the property returns an error. If the tree control contains no items, this
       property returns an error.

       This property returns the tag and column of the item string at the top left corner of the
        visible tree window, which is not necessarily the top left element of the tree. To access
       the top left element, wire a value of 0 to the Active Cell:Active Column Number
       property and to the Active Item:Row Number property.

     Elements

      Name     Description

       Node    The value that appears in the top left corner of the tree control.

       Column  The index of the leftmost column of information displayed in the tree control.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


Name     Description

          Value that corresponds to which mouse button the user clicked. Left mouse button is 1,
            right mouse button is 2. Operating systems might assign higher numbers if you have aButton        mouse with more than two buttons. For filter events, you can modify the data returned
         by this event data field.


           Cluster of Booleans that contain platform-independent modifiers. LabVIEW returns all
          platform-dependent modifiers in the PlatMods event data field. For key events, this
          event returns a Boolean indicating if the event occurred on the numeric keypad. For
Mods    mouse events, this event returns a Boolean indicating if the event was a double-click.
          For both events, a Boolean is returned if the platform-independent menu key, such as
           <Ctrl> on Windows or <Command> on macOS, was pressed when the event occurred.
          For filter events, you can modify the data returned by this event data field.


           Cluster of Booleans that contain platform-dependent modifiers. Specifies if platform-
         dependent keys, such as <Ctrl>, <Shift>, <Alt>, <Command>, and <Option> were held
        down when the event was triggered. For filter events, you can modify the data returned
PlatMods         by this event data field. A key can be both a Mod and PlatMod. For example, <Ctrl> is the
          platform-independent menu key on Windows, but you also can use it in platform-
         dependent programming.


Tag      Unique tag of the item on which the event occurred.


          Value corresponding to the part of the cell the user double-clicked.

          0 Text—The text of any item, row header, or column header.

            Background—Area between the text and the cell borders. Because the text fills the
          1
                  cell, the user cannot access this part of the cell.
CellPart
          2 Item Symbol—The symbol for an item.

            Open/Close Symbol—The symbol that appears to the left of an item when that item
          3
            has child items.

          4 Hierarchy Lines—Horizontal and vertical lines to the left of items that outline the

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

Use this event to signal when a drag and drop operation begins from a specific control.
This event is generated only when LabVIEW begins a drag and drop operation on a tree
control. You can use the Start Drag method to begin a drag from other controls.

Event Data Fields

 Name     Description

          Source of the event. LabVIEW UI refers to any built-in user interface event.

 Source
           0            LabVIEW UI


 Type     Type of event that occurred, such as Mouse Down, Value Change, Timeout, and so on.


 Time     Value of the millisecond timer when the event occurred.


 CtlRef     Reference to the control on which the event occurred.


           Coordinates of the location of the mouse click at the time the event occurs. Coordinates Coords           are relative to the drop target's owning pane origin, excluding clusters.


           Value that corresponds to which mouse button the user clicked. Left mouse button is 1,
            right mouse button is 2. Operating systems might assign higher numbers if you have a
 Button
         mouse with more than two buttons. For filter events, you can modify the data returned
          by this event data field.


            Cluster of Booleans that contain platform-independent modifiers. LabVIEW returns all
          platform-dependent modifiers in the PlatMods event data field. For key events, this
          event returns a Boolean indicating if the event occurred on the numeric keypad. For
 Mods
         mouse events, this event returns a Boolean indicating if the event was a double-click.
           For both events, a Boolean is returned if the platform-independent menu key, such as

SubPanelSubPanel

SubPanel Methods

SubPanel Properties
SubPanelSubPanel MethodsMethods


 Method             Description

 Insert VI           Loads a VI in the subpanel control without changing the state of the VI.

 InsertBlockDiagram  Inserts the VI block diagram into the subpanel

                   Unloads the VI in the subpanel control. If no references to the VI remain,
 Remove VI         LabVIEW removes the VI from memory. If references to the VI remain and the
                        VI stays in memory, this method does not change the state of the VI.

InsertInsert VIVI
InsertInsert VIVI

Loads a VI in the subpanel control without changing the state of the VI.

If the front panel of the VI you want to load is open or if you loaded the front panel in
another subpanel control on the same front panel, LabVIEW returns an error, and you
cannot load the front panel in the subpanel control unless the front panel is reentrant.
You also cannot load the front panel of a VI in a remote application instance, and you
cannot load front panels recursively.

LabVIEW also returns an error if you wire a custom control to this method. To wire a
custom control to a subpanel, place the control on the front panel of a VI. Then wire
that VI to the subpanel.

After you use this method, the front panel is in memory. Use the Close Reference
function to close the VI reference. The front panel remains in the subpanel control until

                                                    © National Instruments 8627

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8627 -->

<!--KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8628 ordinal=8628 -->
## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

      you stop the VI that contains the subpanel control. You also can use the Remove VI
      method to unload the VI in the subpanel control.

     Parameters

              Data      Name       Required  Description               type

                               Reference to the VI whose front panel you want to load. You can use the          VI Ref        Yes                         Open VI Reference function to obtain a reference to another VI.


     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this method.


        Data type                                            No return value

         Available in Run-Time Engine                                       Yes

         Available in Real-Time Operating System                             Yes

         Settable when the VI is running                                      Yes

        Loads the front panel into memory                          No

       Need to authenticate before use                            No

        Loads the block diagram into memory                        No

       Remote access allowed                                             Yes

        Scrollbar.vi
   DocDoc MaxMax
   DocDoc MaxMax

     Maximum value of the scrolling range.

      You can set the maximum value of the scrolling range to be less than the minimum
       value if you want the scrolling range to scroll from Doc Max to Doc Min. If you do not
       coerce Doc Max, you can increment the scroll bar value out of the scrolling range by
        clicking the increment arrow. The top or left position of the scroll box determines the
       value of the scroll bar. If Doc Min is 0, Doc Max is 10, and Page Size is 2, the scrolling
      range is 0 to 8.

       This property is similar to the Maximum option on the Data Entry page of the Scrollbar
       Properties dialog box.

     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


        Data type

         Permissions                                                          Read/Write

         Available in Run-Time Engine                                             Yes

         Available in Real-Time Operating System                                  Yes

8640   ni.com

IncrementIncrement
IncrementIncrement

Increment value of the scrolling range. When you click the increment and decrement
arrows, the scroll bar value adds or subtracts the increment value to move the scroll
box toward the arrow that you click.

If you set this property less than or equal to 0, incrementing by clicking the arrows
uses the increment value of 1.

This property is similar to the Increment option on the Data Entry page of the Scrollbar
Properties dialog box.

Remarks

The following table lists the characteristics of this property.

   PagePage SizeSize
   PagePage SizeSize

      Page size of the scrolling range. When you click the spaces between the scroll box and
       the arrows, the scroll bar value changes by the page size.

      The top or left position of the scroll box determines the value of the scroll bar. If Doc
      Min is 0, Doc Max is 10, and Page Size is 2, the scrolling range is 0 to 8. If you set this
       property less than or equal to 0, LabVIEW coerces the value to 1.

       This property is similar to the Page size option on the Data Entry page of the Scrollbar
       Properties dialog box.

   SceneGraphDisplaySceneGraphDisplay MethodsMethods


       Method                 Description

                                   Positions the camera to view all 3D scene objects in the front panel        AutoFocus                             window.

                                 Casts a ray through a 3D scene at the Point coordinate and determines         Pick Model                             which models in the scene intersect with the ray.

                               Given an x and y coordinate, casts a ray through the 3D scene and returns         PickPoint                                the x, y, and z-coordinates of the first object the ray intersects.

                                 Sets coordinates to render the scene in a frustum-shaped view. This         Projection:Frustum                                  projection causes objects farther from the camera to appear smaller.

                                 Sets coordinates to render the scene in a box-shaped view. The distance
         Projection:Orthographic  of the camera from the objects does not affect the size of the objects in
                                      this view.

                                 Sets coordinates to render the scene in a frustum-shaped view, where
                             you specify an angle for the horizontal and vertical viewing fields. This         Projection:Perspective                                  projection causes objects closer to the camera to appear larger in size.
                                  This method is similar to the Projection:Frustum method.

       Redraw               Redraws the 3D scene in the 3D picture control.

        Setup Camera

        WindowToObjectCoords

SetupSetup CameraCamera
SetupSetup CameraCamera

Specifies the position of the camera relative to the scene. This method modifies the
ModelView Matrix.

Parameters

          Data Name          Required  Description          type

 Camera                   Sets the x, y, and z coordinates that define the initial position of the                 Yes Position                 camera. The default coordinate values are [0, 0, -4].


                           Sets the x, y, and z coordinates that define the point in the scene that
 Target          Yes       the camera faces and around which a spherical camera rotates. The
                             default coordinate values are [0, 0, 0].


 Up                        Sets the x, y, and z coordinates that define the axis that the top of the
                 Yes
 Direction               camera faces. The default coordinate values are [0, 1, 0].

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


       Remote access allowed                                                   Yes

    StringsStrings [][]
    StringsStrings [][]

       Array of 1 string or 6 strings. Strings include text for FALSE, TRUE, MIXED, FALSE
       pressed, TRUE pressed, and MIXED pressed.

           If the mixed checkbox contains multiple strings, it always reads and writes six strings. If
       the mixed checkbox does not contain multiple strings, it always reads and writes one
        string.

       This property is similar to the Multiple strings option on the Appearance page of the
      Mixed Checkbox Properties dialog box.

     Elements

      Name    Description

        0         Displays when the value is FALSE.

        1         Displays when the value is TRUE.

        2         Displays when the value is MIXED.

        3         Displays when the value is FALSE and the checkbox is pressed.

        4         Displays when the value is TRUE and the checkbox is pressed.

        5         Displays when the value is MIXED and the checkbox is pressed.

     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


        Data type

         Permissions                                                          Read/Write

   MultiSegmentPipeMultiSegmentPipe

      MultiSegmentPipe Properties


8678   ni.com

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8678 -->

<!--KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8679 ordinal=8679 -->
## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

MultiSegmentPipeMultiSegmentPipe PropertiesProperties

You can create pipes only if you install the LabVIEW Datalogging and Supervisory
Control Module.


 Property  Description

 Colors          Gets or sets the color of the Multi-Segment Pipe control. [2]

 Flange    Gets or sets the depth of the flange that appears on the left end of a pipe network when
 1:Depth  you first place the Multi-Segment Pipe control on the front panel window.

 Flange    Gets or sets the width of the flange that appears on the left end of a pipe network when
 1:Width  you first place the Multi-Segment Pipe control on the front panel window.

 Flange    Gets or sets the depth of the flange that appears on the right end of a pipe network when
 2:Depth  you first place the Multi-Segment Pipe control on the front panel window.

 Flange    Gets or sets the width of the flange that appears on the right end of a pipe network when
 2:Width  you first place the Multi-Segment Pipe control on the front panel window.

 Pipe      Gets or sets the radius of the pipe segments in a pipe network. All pipe segments in a
 Radius    pipe network have the same radius.

ColorsColors [2][2]
ColorsColors [2][2]

Gets or sets the color of the Multi-Segment Pipe control.

The Multi-Segment Pipe control is a Boolean control that uses different colors to
represent TRUE and FALSE values. Therefore, you can change the color of the pipe
network to customize what the pipe network represents. For example, you might use
the color blue to represent cold water and the color red to represent hot water flowing
through the pipe network.

This property uses an array of two clusters, where each cluster contains a color pair, to
represent the TRUE and FALSE values. Each color pair represents the foreground and


                                                    © National Instruments 8679

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8679 -->

<!--KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8680 ordinal=8680 -->
## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

      background color of the control. You can set the color of the Multi-Segment Pipe
       control by wiring an array of two hexadecimal number pairs with the form RRGGBB or
      by wiring an array of two color box constant pairs to the property.

      You also can set the colors interactively.

     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


        Data type

         Permissions                                                          Read/Write

         Available in Run-Time Engine                                             Yes

         Available in Real-Time Operating System                                  Yes

        Loads the front panel into memory                              No

        Loads the block diagram into memory                            No

       Remote access allowed                                                  Yes

   FlangeFlange 1:Depth1:Depth
   FlangeFlange 1:Depth1:Depth

       Gets or sets the depth of the flange that appears on the left end of a pipe network
     when you first place the Multi-Segment Pipe control on the front panel window.

      The flange depth is the distance, in pixels, from the end of the adjoining pipe segment
       to the end of the flange. The maximum flange depth is 50 pixels. The minimum flange
      depth is four pixels. LabVIEW returns an error if you specify a value greater than the
     maximum or less than the minimum flange depth.

      The following illustration shows the flange depth.

8680   ni.com

PipePipe RadiusRadius
PipePipe RadiusRadius

Gets or sets the radius of the pipe segments in a pipe network. All pipe segments in a
pipe network have the same radius.

The pipe radius is the distance, in pixels, between the center of a pipe segment to the
edge of the pipe segment. The maximum pipe radius is one pixel less than the radius of
the narrowest flange. The radius of a flange is equal to the pipe radius plus the flange
width. The minimum pipe radius is five pixels. LabVIEW returns an error if you specify a
pipe radius greater than the maximum or less than the minimum pipe radius.

The following illustration shows the pipe radius.


                                                    © National Instruments 8685

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8685 -->

       the operating system requests a redraw, such as if the window is no longer behind
      another window, LabVIEW redraws the front panel with the current properties instead

   BackgroundBackground ImageImage

       Sets the background image the pane uses. LabVIEW supports BMP, JPEG, and PNG

       This property is similar to the Browse option on the Appearance page of the Pane
       Properties dialog box.

           If you want to use a picture to set the image, use the Picture to Pixmap VI to convert
       the data to an image data cluster before using this method. To use a file to set the

8724   ni.com

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8724 -->

<!--KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8725 ordinal=8725 -->
## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

image, use the Read JPEG File, Read PNG File, or Read BMP File VIs to convert the data
to an image data cluster before using this method.

Elements

 Name     Description

 Image           Reserved for future use. Type

            Specifies the color depth of the image, which is the number of bits to use to describe
 Image           the color of each pixel in the image. Valid values include 1, 4, 8, and 24 bits per pixel. Depth
          Image Depth affects how LabVIEW interprets the values of Image and Colors.

         A 1-D array of bytes that describes the color of each pixel in the image in raster order.
          The value of Image Depth determines how LabVIEW interprets the value of this input.

                   If Image Depth is 24, each pixel has three bytes to describe its color. The first byte for
          each pixel describes the red value, the second byte describes the green value, and the
             third byte describes the blue value.

                   If Image Depth is 8, each pixel has one byte to describe its color. The value of each bit
 Image     corresponds to an element in Colors, which stores 32-bit RGB values where the most-
             significant byte is zero, followed in order by red, green, and blue values. Valid values
            include 0 through 255.

                   If Image Depth is 4, the behavior is similar to when Image Depth is 8 except valid values
             in image include 0 through 15.

                   If Image Depth is 1, any value of zero in Image corresponds to element 0 in Colors. All
           other values correspond to element 1 in Colors.

         An array of bytes in which each bit describes mask information for a pixel. The first byte
            describes the first eight pixels, the second byte describes the next eight pixels, and so
            on. If a bit is zero, LabVIEW draws the corresponding pixel as transparent. If the array is
 Mask
           empty, LabVIEW draws all pixels without transparency. If the array does not contain a bit
             for each pixel in the image, LabVIEW draws any pixels missing from the array without
            transparency.

         An array of RGB color values that correspond to the values in image. The value of Image
 Colors
          Depth determines how LabVIEW interprets the value of this input.


                                                    © National Instruments 8725

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8725 -->

<!--KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8726 ordinal=8726 -->
## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


      Name     Description

                               If Image Depth is 24, LabVIEW ignores this input.

                               If Image Depth is 8, the array can have 256 elements.

                               If Image Depth is 4, the array can have 16 elements.

                               If Image Depth is 1, the array can have 2 elements.

                A cluster that contains coordinates that describe the bounding rectangle in which you
                 want to draw the image. The VI clips the image to the width and height of the rectangle.
                 The bottom and right edges of the rectangle bounds do not contain image pixels.
                    Horizontal coordinates increase to the right, and vertical coordinates increase to the
                  bottom.
         Rectangle
                                • Left—The horizontal coordinate of the left edge of the rectangle.
                                • Top—The vertical coordinate of the top edge of the rectangle.
                                • Right—The horizontal coordinate of the right edge of the rectangle.
                                • Bottom—The vertical coordinate of the bottom edge of the rectangle.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


 Name     Description

 PaneRef   Reference to the pane on which the event occurred.

 Coords

           Value that corresponds to which mouse button the user clicked. Left mouse button is 1,
            right mouse button is 2. Operating systems might assign higher numbers if you have a Button         mouse with more than two buttons. For filter events, you can modify the data returned
          by this event data field.


            Cluster of Booleans that contain platform-independent modifiers. LabVIEW returns all
          platform-dependent modifiers in the PlatMods event data field. For key events, this
          event returns a Boolean indicating if the event occurred on the numeric keypad. For
 Mods    mouse events, this event returns a Boolean indicating if the event was a double-click.
           For both events, a Boolean is returned if the platform-independent menu key, such as
            <Ctrl> on Windows or <Command> on macOS, was pressed when the event occurred.
           For filter events, you can modify the data returned by this event data field.


            Cluster of Booleans that contain platform-dependent modifiers. Specifies if platform-
          dependent keys, such as <Ctrl>, <Shift>, <Alt>, <Command>, and <Option> were held
        down when the event was triggered. For filter events, you can modify the data returned PlatMods
          by this event data field. A key can be both a Mod and PlatMod. For example, <Ctrl> is the
           platform-independent menu key on Windows, but you also can use it in platform-
          dependent programming.

Name       Description

CtlRef       Reference to the control on which the event occurred.


             Coordinates of the mouse at the time of the event. Coordinates are relative to theCoords              origin of the pane


           The distance the mouse wheel moved. (Windows) A positive value indicates a forward
              rotation of the wheel away from you. A negative value indicates a backward rotation
Delta         of the wheel towards you. (macOS) Navigate to the system settings of the computer
             to specify how the operating system interprets the direction of the mouse wheel
                scroll. macOS 10.7 and later inverts the scroll direction of the mouse by default.


             Value that corresponds to the orientation of the scroll bar and indicates whether the
Orientation             user initiated this event on a horizontal or vertical scroll bar.


              Cluster of Booleans that corresponds to the mouse button(s) the user pressed and
ButtonMods held during the mouse wheel movement. The Booleans indicate whether the user
            pressed the left, right, or middle button(s).


              Cluster of Booleans that contain platform-independent modifiers. LabVIEW returns all
            platform-dependent modifiers in the PlatMods event data field. For key events, this
            event returns a Boolean indicating if the event occurred on the numeric keypad. For
Mods      mouse events, this event returns a Boolean indicating if the event was a double-click.

      Name       Description

                       Cluster of Booleans that contain platform-dependent modifiers. Specifies if platform-

   PanePane SizeSize

      Generated when the user sizes the pane by clicking and dragging the window frame,
        clicking and dragging a splitter bar, maximizing the front panel, or when the user
       restores the pane to its original size from a maximized state.

      Use this event when you want to perform computations necessary for resizing. You can
      use the OldBnds and NewBnds event data field values to determine how the user
       resized the pane.

      Because LabVIEW may generate multiple Pane Size events while you resize the pane,
      LabVIEW generates a final event at the end of the resizing operation in which OldBnds
      and NewBnds return the same value. You can use the values to identify in the code
     when the sizing operation finishes.

     Event Data Fields

      Name     Description

                  Source of the event. LabVIEW UI refers to any built-in user interface event.

        Source
                  0            LabVIEW UI


        Type     Type of event that occurred, such as Mouse Down, Value Change, Timeout, and so on.


8744   ni.com

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8744 -->

<!--KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8745 ordinal=8745 -->
## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


 Name     Description

 Time      Value of the millisecond timer when the event occurred.


 PaneRef   Reference to the pane on which the event occurred.


           Returns a cluster of coordinates in pixels that specify the location of the pane before the
 OldBnds  user resized the pane. Coordinates refer to the upper left and lower right position of the
           pane.


           Returns a cluster of coordinates in pixels that specify the location of the pane after the
 NewBnds  user resized the pane. Coordinates refer to the upper left and lower right position of the
           pane.

SplitterSplitter

Splitter Properties

Splitter Events
SplitterSplitter PropertiesProperties


 Property  Description

 Colors     Colors of the splitter bar in a (Foreground Color, Background Color) pair.


                                                    © National Instruments 8747

<!--END_KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8747 -->

<!--KB_RECORD source=NI_LABVIEW_PROGRAMMING_REFERENCE locator=page:8748 ordinal=8748 -->
## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


        Property  Description

         Colors:BG                     Specifies the background color of the splitter bar.         Color

         Colors:FG                     Specifies the foreground color of the splitter bar.         Color

           Is          Indicates whether the splitter pane is vertical. This property is TRUE if the splitter pane
          Vertical?    is vertical and FALSE if it is horizontal.

         Label     Reference to the label object.

                  Determines the splitter bar behavior when you resize its owner. The owner of a splitter         Sizing
                   bar can be the window or another splitter bar.

                    Controls the position of the splitter. If the splitter is vertical, the position is the          Splitter                     horizontal coordinate of the left of the splitter. If the splitter is horizontal, the position is         Position
                   the vertical coordinate of the top of the splitter.

          Splitter
         Position   Locks the splitter bar so that it cannot be moved by the user.
        Locked

    ColorsColors

       Colors of the splitter bar in a (Foreground Color, Background Color) pair.

      You can set the color of the splitter bar by wiring an numeric constant with the
       representation of U32 with the form RRGGBB or the color box constant to the property.
       This property is similar to using the color picker to specify the foreground and
      background colors of the splitter.

           Note Not all splitter styles display both the foreground and background
                colors. You can change the splitter style of a splitter bar by right-clicking the
                 splitter bar and selecting Splitter Style from the shortcut menu.

     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this property.

    SplitterSplitter PositionPosition

       Controls the position of the splitter. If the splitter is vertical, the position is the
       horizontal coordinate of the left of the splitter. If the splitter is horizontal, the position
         is the vertical coordinate of the top of the splitter.

       Wiring a value to this property positions the splitter at the new location as if you had
     moved the splitter by hand. If the new position violates the minimum size of any pane,
      LabVIEW returns an error and the splitter does not move. This property is similar to
       dragging the splitter bar to the front panel position you want.

     Remarks

      The following table lists the characteristics of this property.


        Data type

8752   ni.com

SplitterSplitter PositionPosition LockedLocked

Locks the splitter bar so that it cannot be moved by the user.

If TRUE, the user cannot move the splitter bar. If FALSE, the user can freely move the
splitter bar by clicking on it and dragging it.

This property is similar to selecting Locked from the shortcut menu.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


 Name      Description

 Time       Value of the millisecond timer when the event occurred.


 SplitterRef Reference to the splitter on which the event occurred.


            Coordinates of the mouse at the location of the mouse click at the time of the event. Coords            Coordinates are relative to the upper left corner of the front panel.


            Value that corresponds to which mouse button the user clicked. Left mouse button is 1,
              right mouse button is 2. Operating systems might assign higher numbers if you have a Button
          mouse with more than two buttons. For filter events, you can modify the data returned
           by this event data field.


             Cluster of Booleans that contain platform-independent modifiers. LabVIEW returns all
            platform-dependent modifiers in the PlatMods event data field. For key events, this
            event returns a Boolean indicating if the event occurred on the numeric keypad. For
 Mods     mouse events, this event returns a Boolean indicating if the event was a double-click.
            For both events, a Boolean is returned if the platform-independent menu key, such as
             <Ctrl> on Windows or <Command> on macOS, was pressed when the event occurred.
            For filter events, you can modify the data returned by this event data field.


             Cluster of Booleans that contain platform-dependent modifiers. Specifies if platform-
           dependent keys, such as <Ctrl>, <Shift>, <Alt>, <Command>, and <Option> were held
         down when the event was triggered. For filter events, you can modify the data returned
 PlatMods
           by this event data field. A key can be both a Mod and PlatMod. For example, <Ctrl> is
            the platform-independent menu key on Windows, but you also can use it in platform-
           dependent programming.

             Coordinates of the mouse at the time of the event. Coordinates are relative to the Coords            upper left corner of the front panel.


            The distance the mouse wheel moved. (Windows) A positive value indicates a forward
               rotation of the wheel away from you. A negative value indicates a backward rotation
 Delta         of the wheel towards you. (macOS) Navigate to the system settings of the computer
              to specify how the operating system interprets the direction of the mouse wheel
                 scroll. macOS 10.7 and later inverts the scroll direction of the mouse by default.


             Value that corresponds to the orientation of the scroll bar and indicates whether the
 Orientation
              user initiated this event on a horizontal or vertical scroll bar.


               Cluster of Booleans that corresponds to the mouse button(s) the user pressed and
 ButtonMods held during the mouse wheel movement. The Booleans indicate whether the user
             pressed the left, right, or middle button(s).

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


       Method               Description

                           Moves the selected objects within this TopLevelDiagram by the number of
                                   pixels specified in X/Y Delta. This method simulates a mouse drag, and it
                             has the same side effects associated with mouse-dragging in the
       Move Selected Objects  development environment, including resizing an owner to contain the
                             dragged objects, altering the selection list to include objects duplicated by
                               the drag, and forcing a duplicate-drag when moving objects to another
                               block diagram.

       Move Selection                           Moves the selected object(s) one step back in the z-plane order.
        Backward

       Move Selection                           Moves the selected object(s) one step forward in the z-plane order.        Forward

       Move Selection To                           Moves the selected objects to the back of the z-plane order.        Back

       Move Selection To                           Moves the selected objects to the front of the z-plane order.         Front

        RemoveFromSelection Removes a selected set of objects from the selection list.

   AlignAlign SelectionSelection

       Aligns selected objects.

         Align Type            Yes              • Bottom Edges

   EncloseEnclose SelectionSelection 22
   EncloseEnclose SelectionSelection 22

       Encloses the selected items on the block diagram in a structure. When you use this
       property to drop a loop, LabVIEW creates tunnels with as few broken wires as possible
      and creates shift register pairs if appropriate.

     Parameters

                      Data
      Name              Required  Description
                      type

                                           Specifies the type of structure to use to enclose the selected
                                          items. This input must be a valid reference to an existing
        EnclosureType        Yes        structure. However, the structure you reference can be located in
                                    any VI and does not need to be on the block diagram where you
                                  want to enclose selected items.

   MoveMove SelectedSelected ObjectsObjects
   MoveMove SelectedSelected ObjectsObjects

      Moves the selected objects within this TopLevelDiagram by the number of pixels
       specified in X/Y Delta. This method simulates a mouse drag, and it has the same side
        effects associated with mouse-dragging in the development environment, including
        resizing an owner to contain the dragged objects, altering the selection list to include
       objects duplicated by the drag, and forcing a duplicate-drag when moving objects to
      another block diagram.

     Parameters

                  Data      Name           Required  Description
                   type

         X/Y Delta       No      Moves the selected objects the number of pixels specified in X and Y.


                               Moves objects such that they are all owned by the object specified in
      New                    No         this parameter. If you do not specify a new owner with this parameter,       Owner                                                all objects stay within their current owner.


         Duplicate?      No        Creates a copy of the moved objects.

        Connect   Connects a wire to the terminal. The wire source can be either another terminal or a
        Wire      node.

         Create     Creates a constant for the terminal and returns a reference to it. You can specify an
        Constant   optional value for the constant.

         Create     Creates a control for the terminal and returns a reference to it. You can specify an
         Control    optional value for the control.

                  Connects a wire from the referenced terminal to the Wire Source terminal, which must
         Create    be a terminal reference. If a wire already exists between the two terminals, this method
        Described  leaves the wire unchanged and does not return an error. If the two terminals are in
        Wire        different subdiagrams and the Wire Description array is not empty, this method returns
                     error 1062.

         Create     Creates an indicator for the terminal and returns a reference to it. You can specify an
         Indicator   optional value for the indicator.

      be a terminal reference. If a wire already exists between the two terminals, this
      method leaves the wire unchanged and does not return an error. If the two terminals
       are in different subdiagrams and the Wire Description array is not empty, this method
       returns error 1062.

     Parameters

                   Data      Name            Required  Description                    type

        Wire                           Yes      The starting point of the new wire.
        Source


                               A 1D array of points describing each tack point along the wire path.
                                The wire starts at Wire Source terminal, proceeds through each of
                                    the points in the array, and terminates at the referenced terminal. Do
                                   not include the locations of the two terminals in the array of points.
        Wire                     Each point is a cluster of the vertical and horizontal coordinates. If                           Yes
         Description               you list every point as a straight vertical or horizontal move from the
                                     previous point, the wire follows that exact route. If you list points
                                       that are diagonal jumps, LabVIEW draws a right angle path from the
                                     previous point to the next one, moving horizontally and then
                                              vertically.


                                    Ignored unless the Wire Description array is empty. If TRUE,
        Auto                     LabVIEW automatically finds the best path for the wire. If FALSE,                    No        Route? (F)                 LabVIEW draws a two-segment wire between the two terminals,
                                moving horizontally and then vertically.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


 Method     Description

 Change to  Changes the constant to a control and returns a reference to the control. LabVIEW
 Control     automatically closes the reference to the constant.

 Change to  Changes the constant to an indicator and returns a reference to the indicator. LabVIEW
 Indicator    automatically closes the reference to the constant.

 Change to  Changes the constant to a Shared Variable node and returns a reference to the Shared
 Shared      Variable node. If you do not specify a shared variable to bind to the node, LabVIEW
 Variable    creates a new shared variable. LabVIEW automatically closes the reference to the
 Node       constant.

 Copy Data  Copies the data associated with the constant and saves it to the clipboard.

 Disconnect            Disconnects the constant from the type definition and returns TRUE. If the constant is From            not connected to a type definition, LabVIEW returns FALSE.
 Typedef

 Paste Data  Places the data from the clipboard into the constant.

 Update           Updates the constant from the type definition and returns TRUE. If the constant is not From            connected to a type definition, LabVIEW returns FALSE.
 Typedef

ChangeChange toto ControlControl

Changes the constant to a control and returns a reference to the control. LabVIEW
automatically closes the reference to the constant.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference

 Available in Run-Time Engine                              No

 Available in Real-Time Operating System                      No

 Settable when the VI is running                             No

 Loads the front panel into memory                          No

 Need to authenticate before use                            No

 Loads the block diagram into memory                        No

 Remote access allowed                                             Yes

UpdateUpdate FromFrom TypedefTypedef

Updates the constant from the type definition and returns TRUE. If the constant is not
connected to a type definition, LabVIEW returns FALSE.

In most cases, LabVIEW correctly preserves the default values of each instance when
updating from the type definition. However, if LabVIEW is unable to map the previous
default values to the updated controls or constants when updating instances, LabVIEW
may lose or incorrectly preserve the default values of instances LabVIEW updates
programmatically. Avoid updating type definition instances programmatically if the
instances have custom default values and you plan to make extensive changes to the
type definition.

Remarks

The following table lists the characteristics of this method.


 Data type

 Available in Run-Time Engine                                         No


                                                    © National Instruments 8839

        Property       Description

        Auto-Update                                        If TRUE, the constant automatically updates when the type definition changes.       From Typedef

         Description     Provides a description of the constant.

           Is Typedef?     Returns whether the constant is linked to the type definition.

         Label          Returns a reference to the label.

        Terminal       Returns a reference to the terminal.

                        Gets or sets the tip strip of a constant. A tip strip is the brief description of the
                         object that appears when you move the cursor over the object.         Tip Strip
                       Other products refer to tip strips as tooltips.

                        Returns the path to the type definition if the constant is linked to a type definition.
         Typedef:Path
                        Otherwise, LabVIEW returns an empty path.

                        Returns a reference to the type definition if the constant is connected to a type
         Typedef:VI                            definition. Otherwise, LabVIEW returns <NotARef>.

         Value           Provides the value of the constant, which is an LV Variant.

   Auto-UpdateAuto-Update FromFrom TypedefTypedef

           If TRUE, the constant automatically updates when the type definition changes.

PathPath TooToo LongLong ToTo FitFit

applies the value of this property only if the scrollbar of the constant is hidden.

You also can use the Path too long to fit pull-down menu on the Appearance page of
the Properties dialog box to specify how to display long paths.

NumericConstantNumericConstant

NumericConstant Properties
NumericConstantNumericConstant PropertiesProperties


 Property                     Description

                                                 If TRUE, the numeric constant changes data type to accommodate
 Adapt To Entered Data        any value you enter. For example, an I32 constant will change to a
                        DBL constant if you enter a fractional value.

 Fixed-Point Overflow Status    Reads or writes whether the overflow status of the fixed-point
 Visible?                  number is visible.

 Fixed-Point                 Reads the actual range of the fixed-point value based on its
 Representation:Actual         encoding.

 Fixed-Point                 Reads the actual delta of the fixed-point value based on its
 Representation:Actual:Delta    encoding.

 Fixed-Point
                           Reads the actual maximum of the fixed-point value based on its Representation:Actual:Range                              encoding.
 Max

 Fixed-Point
                           Reads the actual minimum of the fixed-point value based on its
 Representation:Actual:Range
                              encoding.
 Min

 Fixed-Point                 Reads or writes the encoding of the fixed-point value. Using this
 Representation:Bits           property with non-fixed-point controls will cause an error.

 Fixed-Point                 Reads or writes the integer word length of the fixed-point value.
 Representation:Bits:Integer    Using this property with a non-fixed-point numeric will result in an
 Word Length                     error.

 Fixed-Point                 Reads or writes whether the fixed-point value is a signed value.
 Representation:Bits:Signed    FALSE means unsigned. Using this property with a non-fixed-point

numeric object is a number that corresponds to the values in the following section.

   TextText
    TextText

       Returns a reference to the Text object that represents the text displayed in the
       referenced constant. Unlike with the Value property, you can use this reference with
       the Text properties and methods to manipulate the cosmetic attributes of the text,
      such as the font, color, and size.

## Property and Method Reference

Property and Method Reference


 Property       Description

                          If the control is set to physical channel, indicates the type of signals that the
                 control will display. 1 - AI, 2 - AO, 4 - DI, 8 - DO, 16 - CI, 32 - CO, 64 - Switch, 128 -
                   Internal. In order to have the control display multiple signal types, add the desired
              numbers together. In other words, for AI and CO to be displayed, pass 33 (32 + 1)
                  into the node.

 Switch:Show    Indicates whether to display the switch channels in the pull-down menu of the
 Channels     name control. Use this property only if the control is a DAQmx switch control.

 Switch:Show    Indicates whether to display the switch relays in the pull-down menu of the name
 Relays           control. Use this property only if the control is a DAQmx switch control.

 Switch:Show    Indicates whether to display the switch topologies in the pull-down menu of the
 Topologies    name control. Use this property only if the control is a DAQmx switch control.

                 Indicates whether to display advanced and rarely used terminals in the pull-down Terminal:Show            menu of the control. Use this property only if the control is a DAQmx Terminal Advanced
                  control.

                 Indicates whether to display basic and commonly used terminals in the pull-down Terminal:Show
            menu of the control. Use this property only if the control is a DAQmx Terminal Basic                  control.

NodeNode

Node Methods

Node Properties
NodeNode MethodsMethods


 Method  Description

         Connects wires to the node. The wire source can be either another node or a terminal.
         Auto wire applies only if the source is a node. If auto wire is TRUE, compatible terminals Connect          are chosen automatically from the source node to be wired to the terminals of the node.
 Wires          Wiring specs is a 2D array of strings that specify the names of the source and sink
          terminal pairs.

 Get          Returns an image of a block diagram node. Image

ConnectConnect WiresWires

Connects wires to the node. The wire source can be either another node or a terminal.
Auto wire applies only if the source is a node. If auto wire is TRUE, compatible
terminals are chosen automatically from the source node to be wired to the terminals
of the node. Wiring specs is a 2D array of strings that specify the names of the source
and sink terminal pairs.


                                                    © National Instruments 8961

          (T)                    node.
